        <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Metzger" title="Kelly Metzger">
         Kelly Metzger
        </a>
        in all other appearances), a "spirited competitor" and "no-nonsense instructor" at the Wonderbolts' training academy,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
         <a href="#cite_note-84">
          [83]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
         <a href="#cite_note-85">
          [84]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and her second-in-command Soarin (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hill" title="Matt Hill">
         Matt Hill
        </a>
        ). Their costumes were designed by
        <a href="/wiki/Craig_McCracken" title="Craig McCracken">
         Craig McCracken
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
         <a href="#cite_note-86">
          [85]
         </a>
        </sup>
        According to writer
        <a href="/wiki/Amy_Keating_Rogers" title="Amy Keating Rogers">
         Amy Keating Rogers
        </a>
        , the name of the Wonderbolts' founder, General Firefly, is a tribute to Faust's online username "fyre-flye", in turn named after the "G1" toy Firefly.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
         <a href="#cite_note-87">
          [86]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Hoops">
         </span>
         <span id="Dumb-Bell">
         </span>
         <span id="Billy">
         </span>
         <span id="Score">
         </span>
         <span id="Boy_Bullies">
          Boy Bullies
         </span>
        </b>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
         <a href="#cite_note-88">
          [87]
         </a>
        </sup>
        – A trio of pegasus stallions introduced in "Sonic Rainboom" serve as Rainbow Dash's childhood bullies. They consist of Hoops (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Barr" title="Kathleen Barr">
         Kathleen Barr
        </a>
        in "Sonic Rainboom" and
        <a href="/wiki/Terry_Klassen" title="Terry Klassen">
         Terry Klassen
        </a>
        in all other appearances)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb1_89-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-bb1-89">
          [88]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb2_90-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-bb2-90">
          [89]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and two nameless ponies nicknamed "Billy/Dumb-Bell" (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ian_Cox" title="Richard Ian Cox">
         Richard Ian Cox
        </a>
        in "Sonic Rainboom" and
        <a href="/wiki/Brian_Drummond" title="Brian Drummond">
         Brian Drummond
        </a>
        in "The Cutie Mark Chronicles")
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb1_89-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-bb1-89">
          [88]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb2_90-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-bb2-90">
          [89]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and the unvoiced "Score".
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_antagonists">
        Major antagonists
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Major antagonists">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Nightmare Moon
        </b>
        (see
        <a href="#Princess_Luna">
         Princess Luna
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Discord
        </b>
        (see
        <a href="#Discord">
         above
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Thorax">
         </span>
         <span id="Queen_Chrysalis">
          Queen Chrysalis
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Barr" title="Kathleen Barr">
         Kathleen Barr
        </a>
        ) – Chrysalis is the leader of the
        <a href="/wiki/Changeling" title="Changeling">
         changelings
        </a>
        , a race of "grotesque shape-shifting ponies" that gain power by feeding off of ponies' love for each other.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH53_91-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH53-91">
          [90]
         </a>
        </sup>
        She appears as the antagonist of "
        <a href="/wiki/A_Canterlot_Wedding" title="A Canterlot Wedding">
         A Canterlot Wedding
        </a>
        ", where she leads an invasion of Canterlot by impersonating Princess Cadance to control her fiancé Shining Armor, only for the changelings to be driven off by the couple's combined magic. She also features in "To Where and Back Again", where she is deposed by Thorax (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Rideout" title="Kyle Rideout">
         Kyle Rideout
        </a>
        ), a benevolent changeling who persuades the rest of their kind to share love rather than steal it. Chrysalis makes additional appearances in the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_(comic_book)" title="My Little Pony: Friendship Is Magic (comic book)">
         comic series
        </a>
        , seeking revenge against the ponies responsible for her defeat from the television series. Character designer Rebecca Dart drew Chrysalis and the other changelings with an insect-like design after reading the character's name in the script, drawing inspiration from
        <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">
         manga
        </a>
        artists
        <a href="/wiki/Junko_Mizuno" title="Junko Mizuno">
         Junko Mizuno
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Hideshi_Hino" title="Hideshi Hino">
         Hideshi Hino
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
         <a href="#cite_note-92">
          [91]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="King_Sombra">
          King Sombra
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by Jim Miller) – Sombra is the antagonist of "
        <a href="/wiki/The_Crystal_Empire" title="The Crystal Empire">
         The Crystal Empire
        </a>
        ". Described as a "snarling black-hearted monster", he is a tyrant unicorn king said to have enslaved the crystal ponies until Celestia and Luna banished him as a shadowy mass during Equestria's history.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH53_91-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH53-91">
          [90]
         </a>
        </sup>
        His efforts to reclaim the Crystal Empire are thwarted when he is destroyed by the magical Crystal Heart that protects the city. The comics explore Sombra's role as an "umbrum", a shadow pony who embraced his kind's monstrous nature after being rejected by the crystal ponies, only to be restored to life and redeemed by Radiant Hope, his childhood friend. Miller based his performance on the vocals of
        <a href="/wiki/Mastodon_(band)" title="Mastodon (band)">
         Mastodon
        </a>
        song "Crystal Skull".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
         <a href="#cite_note-93">
          [92]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Lord_Tirek">
          Lord Tirek
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Mark_Acheson" title="Mark Acheson">
         Mark Acheson
        </a>
        ) – Tirek is a red-skinned,
        <a href="/wiki/Bull" title="Bull">
         bull
        </a>
        -like
        <a href="/wiki/Centaur" title="Centaur">
         centaur
        </a>
        who appears as the antagonist of "
        <a href="/wiki/Twilight%27s_Kingdom" title="Twilight's Kingdom">
         Twilight's Kingdom
        </a>
        ". Based on the character of the same name from the animated
        <a href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony" title="My Little Pony">
         My Little Pony
        </a>
        special
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Rescue_at_Midnight_Castle" title="Rescue at Midnight Castle">
          Rescue at Midnight Castle
         </a>
        </i>
        , he is depicted in
        <i>
         Friendship Is Magic
        </i>
        as an ancient and diabolical tyrant who escapes from the prison realm of
        <a href="/wiki/Tartarus" title="Tartarus">
         Tartarus
        </a>
        , manipulating Discord to help him steal all magic from Equestria's ponies. The Mane Six eventually defeat and reimprison him with their "Rainbow Power", a more formidable magic acquired from the Tree of Harmony. Character designer Phil Caesar strove to make Tirek appear as intimidating as he could without being deemed "too scary" for younger audiences, giving him design elements such as a black upper body to "tone down the intensity".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
         <a href="#cite_note-94">
          [93]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Starlight Glimmer
        </b>
        (see
        <a href="#Starlight_Glimmer">
         above
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Stygian">
         </span>
         <span id="Pony_of_Shadows">
          Pony of Shadows
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by Bill Newton) – First mentioned in "Castle Mane-ia" as the subject of a
        <a href="/wiki/Ghost_story" title="Ghost story">
         ghost story
        </a>
        , the Pony of Shadows serves as the antagonist of "Shadow Play". He is the alter ego of Stygian, a resentful unicorn who is mistaken for a traitor and shunned by his allies, the Pillars of Old Equestria, and bonded with a malevolent entity that takes the form of a shadowy, alicorn-like monster. He is inadvertently freed alongside the Pillars by the Mane Six, thwarting the heroes' millennium-long effort to contain him in
        <a href="/wiki/Limbo" title="Limbo">
         limbo
        </a>
        . Stygian's innocence is eventually recognized by the Pillars, who work alongside the Mane Six to separate him from the shadow creature, which is returned to limbo in his place.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_recurring_characters">
        Other recurring characters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other recurring characters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Gilda">
          Gilda
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Maryke_Hendrikse" title="Maryke Hendrikse">
         Maryke Hendrikse
        </a>
        ) – Gilda is a female
        <a href="/wiki/Griffin" title="Griffin">
         griffon
        </a>
        featured in the season one episode "Griffon the Brush Off". She is introduced as a childhood friend of Rainbow Dash, who later ends their friendship when Gilda tries to assert herself over Rainbow Dash's pony friends by bullying them.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH55_95-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH55-95">
          [94]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The two later reconnect in the season five episode "The Lost Treasure of Griffonstone".
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Trixie_Lulamoon">
         </span>
         <span id="Trixie">
          Trixie
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Barr" title="Kathleen Barr">
         Kathleen Barr
        </a>
        ) – Trixie is a traveling unicorn
        <a href="/wiki/Magic_(illusion)" title="Magic (illusion)">
         magician
        </a>
        and braggart who exaggerates her magical abilities, calling herself "The Great and Powerful Trixie". She makes appearances in the show and various spin-offs as either an anti-hero or villain,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
         <a href="#cite_note-96">
          [95]
         </a>
        </sup>
        beginning as a rival to Twilight Sparkle in the season one episode "Boast Busters", but becoming more apologetic after seeing the error of her vengeful actions in season three's "Magic Duel".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH55_95-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH55-95">
          [94]
         </a>
        </sup>
        She appears in various episodes during seasons six and seven, forming a friendship with Starlight Glimmer, another reformed unicorn.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Garble">
         </span>
         <span id="Dragon_Lord_Torch">
         </span>
         <span id="Princess_Ember">
         </span>
         <span id="Dragons">
          Dragons
         </span>
        </b>
        – The
        <a href="/wiki/Dragon" title="Dragon">
         dragons
        </a>
        that appear throughout the series are generally depicted as selfish and reclusive creatures, and their level of greed determines their size and physical maturity.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
         <a href="#cite_note-97">
          [96]
         </a>
        </sup>
        They are governed by a Dragon Lord, the gargantuan Torch (voiced by Matt Cowlrick), who is succeeded by his moody yet compassionate daughter, Princess Ember (voiced by Ali Milner), in the season six episode "Gauntlet of Fire". A teenage dragon, Garble (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Tong" title="Vincent Tong">
         Vincent Tong
        </a>
        ), leads a gang of "bad-natured bullies" and becomes an adversary of Spike.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
         <a href="#cite_note-98">
          [97]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Begin describes the dragon designs used in the show as "traditional", while finding that their "exaggerated noses and large heads resting on exceptionally skinny necks" is evocative of the show's humor.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
         <a href="#cite_note-99">
          [98]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Zecora">
          Zecora
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by Brenda Crichlow) – Zecora is a
        <a href="/wiki/Zebra" title="Zebra">
         zebra
        </a>
        shaman and herbalist who always speaks in rhyme and lives in the Everfree Forest, a "mysterious" forest on the edge of Ponyville.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
         <a href="#cite_note-100">
          [99]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The townsfolk misjudge her as an "evil enchantress" until the Mane Six befriend her in the episode "Bridle Gossip", often turning to her for her wisdom afterwards.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
         <a href="#cite_note-101">
          [100]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Her appearance and mannerisms are influenced by
        <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Africa" title="Culture of Africa">
         African tribal cultures
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
         <a href="#cite_note-102">
          [101]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Aunt_and_Uncle_Orange">
         </span>
         <span id="Auntie_Applesauce_and_Apple_Rose">
         </span>
         <span id="Braeburn">
         </span>
         <span id="Goldie_Delicious">
         </span>
         <span id="Hayseed_Turnip_Truck">
         </span>
         <span id="Apple_family">
          Apple family
         </span>
        </b>
        – The Apples are Applejack's
        <a href="/wiki/Extended_family" title="Extended family">
         extended family
        </a>
        of earth ponies that live throughout Equestria. Family members include Braeburn (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Michael_Daingerfield" title="Michael Daingerfield">
         Michael Daingerfield
        </a>
        ), Applejack's cousin from Appleloosa, a "
        <a href="/wiki/American_frontier" title="American frontier">
         Wild West
        </a>
        " town;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH28_70-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH28-70">
          [69]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH72_103-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH72-103">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
        her "high-society" Aunt and Uncle Orange (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Tabitha_St._Germain" title="Tabitha St. Germain">
         Tabitha St. Germain
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Brian_Drummond" title="Brian Drummond">
         Brian Drummond
        </a>
        ) from the "bustling city" of Manehattan;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH72_103-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH72-103">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Hayseed Turnip Truck (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Devall" title="Trevor Devall">
         Trevor Devall
        </a>
        ), a
        <a href="/wiki/Yokel" title="Yokel">
         yokel
        </a>
        -type odd-job worker; Babs Seed (see
        <a href="#Cutie_Mark_Crusaders">
         Cutie Mark Crusaders
        </a>
        ); Auntie Applesauce and Apple Rose (voiced by St. Germain and
        <a href="/wiki/Ashleigh_Ball" title="Ashleigh Ball">
         Ashleigh Ball
        </a>
        ), two older relatives and friends of Granny Smith; Goldie Delicious (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Peter_New" title="Peter New">
         Peter New
        </a>
        ), an old
        <a href="/wiki/Cat_lady" title="Cat lady">
         cat lady
        </a>
        who hoards family heirlooms; and Grand Pear (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">
         William Shatner
        </a>
        ), Applejack's maternal grandfather and patriarch of the rival Pear family. A possible distant relationship between the Apple and Pie families is uncovered in the season four episode "Pinkie Apple Pie", but is never confirmed.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Igneous_Rock">
         </span>
         <span id="Cloudy_Quartz">
         </span>
         <span id="Maud_Pie">
         </span>
         <span id="Limestone_Pie">
         </span>
         <span id="Marble_Pie">
         </span>
         <span id="Pie_family">
          Pie family
         </span>
        </b>
        – The Pies are Pinkie Pie's family who live on a rock farm outside of Ponyville. They are depicted as a clan of dour, drably colored earth ponies in contrast to Pinkie's bright appearance and personality.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH-CMC_53-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH-CMC-53">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
        They consist of Pinkie's father Igneous Rock (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Terry_Klassen" title="Terry Klassen">
         Terry Klassen
        </a>
        in "
        <a href="/wiki/The_Cutie_Mark_Chronicles" title="The Cutie Mark Chronicles">
         The Cutie Mark Chronicles
        </a>
        " and Peter New in "Hearthbreakers"), mother Cloudy Quartz (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Libman" title="Andrea Libman">
         Andrea Libman
        </a>
        in "Hearthbreakers"), and three sisters (all voiced by Ingrid Nilson): Limestone Pie, the surly oldest sister; Marble Pie, Pinkie's withdrawn, younger twin; and Maud Pie, an older sister who rarely expresses emotion and is obsessed with rocks, introduced in the show's fourth season.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Starswirl_the_Bearded">
         </span>
         <span id="Star_Swirl_the_Bearded">
          Star Swirl the Bearded
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Britton_(actor)" title="Christopher Britton (actor)">
         Christopher Britton
        </a>
        ) – Star Swirl is a unicorn and historical figure in the series, originally envisioned as an archetypal wizard character with a prominent beard, similar to
        <a href="/wiki/Merlin" title="Merlin">
         Merlin
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
         <a href="#cite_note-104">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
        As detailed in the series and various tie-in media, he mentored Equestria's co-founder Clover the Clever and served as Celestia and Luna's royal adviser in their youth.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jots_45-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-jots-45">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Star Swirl's spellbook is a key figure in "
        <a href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Cure" title="Magical Mystery Cure">
         Magical Mystery Cure
        </a>
        ", where Twilight is directed by Princess Celestia to finish Star Swirl's "unfinished masterpiece" written within, resulting in her ascension as an alicorn princess of Equestria. He is depicted in the seventh season finale "Shadow Play" and the accompanying
        <i>
         Legends of Magic
        </i>
        comic series as the leader of the Pillars of Old Equestria, six legendary ponies responsible for creating the Elements of Harmony. He and the other Pillars are brought into the present era after being released from a millennial imprisonment in
        <a href="/wiki/Limbo" title="Limbo">
         limbo
        </a>
        alongside the Pony of Shadows, forming a tense alliance with the Mane Six to defeat and ultimately rekindle his friendship with the villain.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Flim">
         </span>
         <span id="Flam">
         </span>
         <span id="Flim_Flam_Brothers">
          Flim Flam Brothers
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Vincent" title="Samuel Vincent">
         Samuel Vincent
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Scott_McNeil" title="Scott McNeil">
         Scott McNeil
        </a>
        ) – Flim and his mustachioed brother Flam are two traveling unicorn "salesponies" and
        <a href="/wiki/Confidence_trick" title="Confidence trick">
         con artists
        </a>
        who use song and dance to enthrall ponies into buying their usually faulty wares.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH56_105-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH56-105">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Writer
        <a href="/wiki/M.A._Larson" title="M.A. Larson">
         M.A. Larson
        </a>
        said he "particularly enjoyed" writing for Flim and Flam, saying that "their energy and optimism infuses the actual writing".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH56_105-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH56-105">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="A.K._Yearling">
         </span>
         <span id="Ahuizotl">
         </span>
         <span id="Dr._Caballeron">
         </span>
         <span id="Daring_Do">
          Daring Do
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Chiara_Zanni" title="Chiara Zanni">
         Chiara Zanni
        </a>
        ) – Daring Do is a pegasus and main character of the fictional
        <i>
         Daring Do
        </i>
        adventure novel series parodying
        <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Jones" title="Indiana Jones">
         Indiana Jones
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
         <a href="#cite_note-106">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Author Begin describes her as "essentially a different-colored Rainbow Dash in a hat".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoE188_107-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-AoE188-107">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In the season four episode "Daring Don't", the books' author A.K. Yearling (a parody of
        <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">
         J.K. Rowling
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
         <a href="#cite_note-108">
          [107]
         </a>
        </sup>
        is discovered to be Daring Do herself, who writes her books after her real adventures, such as her encounters with the
        <a href="/wiki/Aztec_mythology" title="Aztec mythology">
         Aztec mythology
        </a>
        -based villain
        <a href="/wiki/Ahuizotl_(creature)" title="Ahuizotl (creature)">
         Ahuizotl
        </a>
        (voiced by Brian Drummond) and criminal pony Dr. Caballeron (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dobson_(actor)" title="Michael Dobson (actor)">
         Michael Dobson
        </a>
        ).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
         <a href="#cite_note-109">
          [108]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Miss_Pommel">
         </span>
         <span id="Coco_Pommel">
          Coco Pommel
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Cathy_Weseluck" title="Cathy Weseluck">
         Cathy Weseluck
        </a>
        ) – Coco is an earth pony fashion designer who works in Manehattan. She is introduced in the season four episode "Rarity Takes Manehattan" as the assistant to Suri Polomare (voiced by Tabitha St. Germain), Rarity's chief rival in a fashion competition, and quits after observing Suri's unscrupulous tactics for winning. Her name is a reference to fashion designer
        <a href="/wiki/Coco_Chanel" title="Coco Chanel">
         Coco Chanel
        </a>
        ; it was later changed to "Miss Pommel" prior to the show's sixth season for "legal reasons".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
         <a href="#cite_note-110">
          [109]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Background_characters">
        Background characters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Background characters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The show features an extensive cast of over 200 minor characters, also designated "background ponies",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoE75_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AoE75-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       that are used to fill out crowd scenes and serve as
       <a href="/wiki/Visual_gag" title="Visual gag">
        visual gags
       </a>
       in episodes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awn_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-awn-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Several background ponies have been well received by the show's
       <a href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_fandom" title="My Little Pony: Friendship Is Magic fandom">
        brony fanbase
       </a>
       , who have assigned names and more detailed personalities to them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awn_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-awn-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a response to fan interest, the series' creative team have given these characters expanded roles in later episodes and media,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoE75_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AoE75-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       such as the show's one-hundredth episode "
       <a href="/wiki/Slice_of_Life_(My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic)" title="Slice of Life (My Little Pony: Friendship Is Magic)">
        Slice of Life
       </a>
       ", which presents the characters' daily lives as the episode's central focus.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoE-9293_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AoE-9293-112">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Derpy">
         </span>
         <span id="Muffins">
         </span>
         <span id="Derpy/Muffins">
          Derpy/Muffins
         </span>
        </b>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S02E14_113-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-S02E14-113">
          [112]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S05E09_114-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-S05E09-114">
          [113]
         </a>
        </sup>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Tabitha_St._Germain" title="Tabitha St. Germain">
         Tabitha St. Germain
        </a>
        ) – "Derpy" is the name assigned to a cross-eyed pegasus who makes several background appearances in the show. Originally the subject of an overlooked animator's joke in the first episode, the character was dubbed "Derpy Hooves" (based on the
        <a href="/wiki/Internet_slang" title="Internet slang">
         Internet slang
        </a>
        word "
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/derp" title="wiktionary:derp">
         derp
        </a>
        ") and characterized as a well-meaning klutz by
        <a href="/wiki/4chan" title="4chan">
         4chan
        </a>
        board users.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awn_3-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-awn-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The creators have since recognized "Derpy" as the fandom's mascot and included her in scripted
        <a href="/wiki/Easter_egg_(media)" title="Easter egg (media)">
         easter eggs
        </a>
        throughout the show.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awn_3-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-awn-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csm_115-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-csm-115">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
        She was addressed by name and given lines during the initial broadcast of the second-season episode "The Last Roundup" as a direct call-out to the fandom. Following complaints from viewers who felt her appearance and actions negatively reflected those of mentally handicapped people, the scene was modified to remove the character's name, alter her voice, and reduce the degree to which her eyes are crossed.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deprygate_116-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-deprygate-116">
          [115]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Amidst concerns that Derpy would be removed from the series due to these responses, the character was re-introduced in the fourth season as a "surprise" for fans after having been reduced to background cameos in previous episodes.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
         <a href="#cite_note-117">
          [116]
         </a>
        </sup>
        According to Miller, the character was renamed "Muffins" for "legal reasons that I don't understand" prior to her credited appearance in "Slice of Life".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
         <a href="#cite_note-118">
          [117]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="DJ_Pon-3">
         </span>
         <span id="Vinyl_Scratch">
         </span>
         <span id="DJ_Pon-3/Vinyl_Scratch">
          DJ Pon-3/Vinyl Scratch
         </span>
        </b>
        – DJ Pon-3 (
        <span class="nowrap">
         <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
          <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
           /
           <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
            <span title="'p' in 'pie'">
             p
            </span>
            <span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">
             oʊ
            </span>
            <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
             n
            </span>
            <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
             ˈ
            </span>
            <span title="/θ/: 'th' in 'thigh'">
             θ
            </span>
            <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
             r
            </span>
            <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
             iː
            </span>
           </span>
           /
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        ) is a silent unicorn
        <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">
         disc jockey
        </a>
        rarely seen without headphones and sunglasses, first seen in "Suited for Success".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH33_77-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH33-77">
          [76]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The names "DJ Pon-3" and "Vinyl Scratch" were created by the fan community, with the former being used in official products, such as the "Equestria Girls" music video parodying
        <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">
         Katy Perry
        </a>
        's song "
        <a href="/wiki/California_Gurls" title="California Gurls">
         California Gurls
        </a>
        ".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bnet_119-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-bnet-119">
          [118]
         </a>
        </sup>
        She also makes major, non-speaking appearances in the film
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Equestria_Girls_%E2%80%93_Rainbow_Rocks" title="My Little Pony: Equestria Girls – Rainbow Rocks">
          My Little Pony: Equestria Girls – Rainbow Rocks
         </a>
        </i>
        and its accompanying shorts.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
         <a href="#cite_note-120">
          [119]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Dr._Hooves">
         </span>
         <span id="Time_Turner">
         </span>
         <span id="Dr._Hooves/Time_Turner">
          Dr. Hooves/Time Turner
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Peter_New" title="Peter New">
         Peter New
        </a>
        ) – An earth pony background character, his name was coined as "Doctor Whooves" by fans for his purported resemblance to
        <a href="/wiki/David_Tennant" title="David Tennant">
         David Tennant
        </a>
        's portrayal of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tenth_Doctor" title="Tenth Doctor">
         Tenth Doctor
        </a>
        in the British television series
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">
          Doctor Who
         </a>
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
         <a href="#cite_note-121">
          [120]
         </a>
        </sup>
        He appears in later episodes as Ponyville's eccentric
        <a href="/wiki/Timekeeper" title="Timekeeper">
         timekeeper
        </a>
        , and he exhibits similarities to his namesake in episodes such as "Slice of Life". He is voiced by various actors besides New, who performs him in his major speaking appearance in "Slice of Life".
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Lyra_Heartstrings">
          Lyra Heartstrings
         </span>
         and
         <span id="Bon_Bon">
         </span>
         <span id="Sweetie_Drops">
         </span>
         <span id="Bon_Bon/Sweetie_Drops">
          Bon Bon/Sweetie Drops
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Ashleigh_Ball" title="Ashleigh Ball">
         Ashleigh Ball
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Libman" title="Andrea Libman">
         Andrea Libman
        </a>
        ) – The unicorn Lyra and earth pony Sweetie Drops (also named Bon Bon after the "G1" pony) are two incidental characters who appear together as best friends in several scenes; one such scene in "Slice of Life" outs Sweetie Drops as a disavowed secret agent living in Ponyville under the assumed identity "Bon Bon". They are voiced by various actresses, with Ball voicing Lyra and Libman as Sweetie Drops in "Slice of Life" and the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Equestria_Girls_%E2%80%93_Friendship_Games" title="My Little Pony: Equestria Girls – Friendship Games">
          Friendship Games
         </a>
        </i>
        film and shorts.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Minuette">
          Minuette
         </span>
         ,
         <span id="Twinkleshine">
          Twinkleshine
         </span>
         , and
         <span id="Lemon_Hearts">
          Lemon Hearts
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by Rebecca Husain, Tabitha St. Germain and Ashleigh Ball) – Often appearing separately as incidental characters, these three unicorns are given focus in the series premiere and season five episode "Amending Fences" as Twilight Sparkle's often neglected friends from before her move to Ponyville, while Minuette and Twinkleshine appear alongside Lyra Heartstrings as Princess Cadance's bridesmaids in "
        <a href="/wiki/A_Canterlot_Wedding" title="A Canterlot Wedding">
         A Canterlot Wedding
        </a>
        ". Among various other actresses, they are voiced by Husain (Minuette), St. Germain (Twinkleshine), and Ball (Lemon Hearts) in "Amending Fences".
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <span id="Octavia">
         </span>
         <span id="Octavia_Melody">
          Octavia Melody
         </span>
        </b>
        (voiced by
        <a href="/wiki/Kazumi_Evans" title="Kazumi Evans">
         Kazumi Evans
        </a>
        ) – Octavia is an earth pony who plays the
        <a href="/wiki/Cello" title="Cello">
         cello
        </a>
        , originally seen in "The Best Night Ever".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoH33_77-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-EoH33-77">
          [76]
         </a>
        </sup>
        She is featured in a scene in "
        <a href="/wiki/Slice_of_Life_(My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic)" title="Slice of Life (My Little Pony: Friendship Is Magic)">
         Slice of Life
        </a>
        " where she rehearses an "electric cello dubstep" number with fellow musician DJ Pon-3 for Cranky and Mathilda's wedding; Octavia's portion of the song was performed by
        <a href="/wiki/Tina_Guo" title="Tina Guo">
         Tina Guo
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
         <a href="#cite_note-122">
          [121]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
        Reception
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Reception">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The characters of
       <i>
        My Little Pony: Friendship Is Magic
       </i>
       have received praise, and are cited as one of the reasons the series' older fans, called "
       <a href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_Is_Magic_fandom" title="My Little Pony: Friendship Is Magic fandom">
        bronies
       </a>
       ", became attracted to the show.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyobserver_origin_123-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nyobserver_origin-123">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In his review of the show, Todd VanDerWerff of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">
         The A.V. Club
        </a>
       </i>
       complimented the characters' stylized appearance and defined personalities, while favorably noting that "the show uses them well to come up with fun stories and bounce solid jokes off of each other."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AVClub_51-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AVClub-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Emily Ashby of
       <a href="/wiki/Common_Sense_Media" title="Common Sense Media">
        Common Sense Media
       </a>
       , an organization focusing on the parenting aspect of children's media, felt the characters posed a positive influence on children with themes tolerance and respect for one another, and that they "don't let their diverse personalities keep them from forging relationships". However, she advised parents to be wary of the "influence the characters might have on their kids' desires, since it's rooted in a well-known product line of books, toys, and just about everything in between."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CommonSenseMedia_124-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CommonSenseMedia-124">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">
         Los Angeles Times
        </a>
       </i>
       critic Robert Lloyd praised the show's diverse female characterization, but noted the smaller male cast by comparison, calling them "largely beside the point."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Kathleen Richter of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ms._(magazine)" title="Ms. (magazine)">
         Ms.
        </a>
       </i>
       was dismissive of the characters in her critique of the show in comparison to other girls' shows, which she considered "so sexist and racist and
       <a href="/wiki/Heteronormativity" title="Heteronormativity">
        heteronormative
       </a>
       ." For example, she suggested that the character of Rainbow Dash was used to promote the stereotype that "all feminists are angry, tomboyish lesbians." She also considered that the only darker-colored ponies shown at the time were in positions of servitude towards the "white pony overlord".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ms_richter_126-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ms_richter-126">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Lauren Faust responded to these claims by stating that while Rainbow Dash was a tomboy, "nowhere in the show is her sexual orientation ever referenced" and "assuming [tomboys] are lesbians is extremely unfair to both straight and lesbian tomboys", and further stating that "Color has never, ever been depicted as a race indicator for the ponies."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ms_faust_2-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-ms_faust-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The portrayal of the character Derpy in the second season episode "The Last Roundup" received a negative response from some viewers, who felt her crossed eyes and klutzy mannerisms were insulting to mentally handicapped persons;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-derpygate_127-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-derpygate-127">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hasbro's subsequent modifications to the scene to reduce such character traits were also received poorly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-derpygate_127-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-derpygate-127">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
